  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1347654230" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1347654230" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41609617-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539156508p2/41609617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1347654230?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/41609617-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347654230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5336514037761203735">Set in a dystopian 21st century near future British society – the ‘Noughts & Crosses’ award winning series of novels (initially a trilogy, subsequently extended to a quadrilogy) opens following a period of alternative history, a post slavery period where the white population (Noughts) have been enslaved by the ruling black elite. Now post emancipation, it is the non-black population who are distinctly disadvantaged and impoverished in this alternative future society which is ruled and controlled</span>
  <span id="freeText5336514037761203735" style="display:none">Set in a dystopian 21st century near future British society – the ‘Noughts &amp; Crosses’ award winning series of novels (initially a trilogy, subsequently extended to a quadrilogy) opens following a period of alternative history, a post slavery period where the white population (Noughts) have been enslaved by the ruling black elite. Now post emancipation, it is the non-black population who are distinctly disadvantaged and impoverished in this alternative future society which is ruled and controlled by the dominating blacks (Crosses).<br /><br />The ‘Noughts &amp; Crosses’ series provides us with an explicit flip and twist on both the history and current political and cultural demographic of British society – where racial politics is turned on its head and power structures are completely reversed. <br /><br />The fundamental premise underlying this series is a vitally important one – what Malorie Blackman seems to have set out to do, is to robustly challenge (what may be many) readers’ current perceptions, presumptions, assumptions and views on race and (British) society. An attempt to provoke thought and to revisit the absurdities of a society(ies) run along lines on racial disadvantagement and the domination of one ethnic group or groups in society by another controlling ethnic (almost always white) group. The books successfully challenge and encourage particularly the non-black reader to reconsider and think again about being part of and party to, a racially privileged white society – and by extension, to consider the real life alternative in the light of the fictional world that is portrayed here in the ‘Noughts &amp; Crosses’ series. Moreover – to consider the possibility of a third way – a society run entirely along non-racially defined power structures. <br /><br />This is an original, intelligent, perceptive and though-provoking series of books – and whilst squarely aimed at the Young Adult market, it clearly transcends the restrictive boundaries of that genre.<br /><br />The first installment ‘Noughts &amp; Crosses’ is the strongest of the series, closely followed by the second and third parts of the original trilogy namely ‘Knife Edge’ and ‘Checkmate’. Whilst ‘Double Cross’ is well-written and ostensibly does add value to the series, it does feel ultimately a little superfluous and does not provide the same impact as the preceding three novels.<br /><br />Moreover, apart from being politically and culturally astute, what makes the ‘Noughts &amp; Crosses’ series of books so successful is not merely the originality and the ever-present / underlying theme of racial politics, but the fact that Blackman has created great characters who inhabit great page-turning stories which are both compelling and engaging.<br /><br />These are increasingly important books to be read by all – particularly in view of the current political climate and the ever more disturbing rise in the so-called ‘alt right’ / white supremacist groups in certain parts of the world. <br /><br />It is very encouraging that Blackman's series of books has been so successful and is widely read and made available in UK schools – as it quite rightly should continue to be.<br /><br />Throughout the course of the ‘Noughts &amp; Crosses’ series of novels, Malorie Blackman successfully shines a light on the absurdities of racial domination and subjugation of one group by another and the fundamental racist agenda (implicit and explicit, covert and overt – at both personal and societal levels) that underpins and perpetuates this ridiculous cultural dialectic.<br /><br />In the words of Nelson Mandela (as recently quoted by Barack Obama): <br /><br /> “No one is born hating another person because of the colour of his skin or his background or his religion…”<br /><br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5336514037761203735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3383786989178595284" style="display:none">A society where citizens are divided based on their skin tones. <b>Noughts</b> are the white citizens, most of them are laboring class and they are controlled by <b>Crosses</b>, who are the black citizens. <span id="freeTextContainer3415957342584117557">Alright, it's been about 24 hours, I'm less emotional, lets review this. <br/><br/>I'm going to start my review with like a fuck-ton of warnings. <br/>Warning 1: I don't honestly feel very comfortable reviewing this, so it's not going to be very in depth. <br/>Warning 2: These are my thoughts based on what I know and who I am, if I am ignorant in any way in this review, please use this as a good time to educate me, not yell at me.<br/>Warning 3: I loved this book a little too much to be fully unbiased. <br/><br/>So, this book fel</span>
  <span id="freeText3415957342584117557" style="display:none">Alright, it's been about 24 hours, I'm less emotional, lets review this. <br /><br />I'm going to start my review with like a fuck-ton of warnings. <br />Warning 1: I don't honestly feel very comfortable reviewing this, so it's not going to be very in depth. <br />Warning 2: These are my thoughts based on what I know and who I am, if I am ignorant in any way in this review, please use this as a good time to educate me, not yell at me.<br />Warning 3: I loved this book a little too much to be fully unbiased. <br /><br />So, this book felt TO ME like a historical fiction retelling/alternate reality. In this book we are essentially in an un-specified time period, but the events follow very similarly to the civil rights era of the late 50s and 60s in the US. But, in this story, the races are switched. You have the noughts, the lesser white race, and the Crosses, the superior black race. <br /><br />This book really just focuses on the story of a black girl and a white boy who have spent their entire lives being friends and are just trying to exist and figure out how to grow up in a world where their interactions are seen as wrong and, on some occasions, even dangerous. And I fucking loved the social commentary in this. <br /><br />Not only are we having so many social commentaries on race relations, we are having commentary on sensitivity, why certain actions and certain comments cause more harm than they are ever intended to. How sometimes "I was just trying to help" just makes things worse. This book, in my opinion, is having the discussions that people are wanting to see in literature lately, but was having them 17 years ago. <br /><br />I appreciate that this was told by an own voices author, someone who I trust would help me understand what people would have felt in this time period, and someone who would tell me things accurately. It also teaches a lot of black history, and does so really smoothly within the plot of the story. <br /><br />Honestly though, the things I took away were really the sensitivity things. Things to say, things not to say. Sometimes, it's really difficult to know what to say because you don't want to upset people, especially when you just don't understand how something feels and have never experienced what others have, and this book had some really good lessons on kind of things to avoid. I recently in another book review complained that an author used a situation in her book and called out racism and rather than teaching, she just straight up yelled at everyone. This book teaches, and I so so so appreciated it. <br /><br />However, all of this comes from a white person. I don't actually know if anything in the book is even accurate, if people feel like the lessons in this book were accurate or spot on. I have read a few own voices reviews that actually seem to agree, but I really recommend reading those in order to get more information on this. <br /><br />But based on the contents of these pages, I just loved every single moment. </span>

<div id="review_67473855" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67473855" />
    <a title="Carolyn  Storer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2449271-carolyn-storer"><img alt="Carolyn  Storer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457826767p2/2449271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67473855?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn  Storer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn  Storer" href="/user/show/2449271-carolyn-storer">Carolyn  Storer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=book-list-2009">book-list-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67473855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17283885881851288669">Wow, this book is outstanding. I couldn't put it down! As someone who is in her thirties, I wondered whether this book would be too young and the writing immature, but this wasn't the case at all. This is an intelligently and sensitively written story about two friends, Callum, a white-skinned nought and Sephy a dark-skinned Cross and their relationship as they grow up. How society and the prejudices around them moulds them into people they don't really want to be. It's a story filled with trage</span>
  <span id="freeText17283885881851288669" style="display:none">Wow, this book is outstanding. I couldn't put it down! As someone who is in her thirties, I wondered whether this book would be too young and the writing immature, but this wasn't the case at all. This is an intelligently and sensitively written story about two friends, Callum, a white-skinned nought and Sephy a dark-skinned Cross and their relationship as they grow up. How society and the prejudices around them moulds them into people they don't really want to be. It's a story filled with tragedy and sorrow but also love and friendship. The story is narrated by both Sephy and Callum alternating with each chapter and allows us to see their very different worlds through their eyes. <br /><br />As a teenager this book would have rocked my world! As much as Why the Caged Bird Sings by Maya Angelou and The Colour Purple by Alice Walker did as an adult. The frustration and anger felt at the injustice of prejudice spawned from just the colour of a persons skin never left me while reading this book. The black and white racism issue is tuned upside down and the dark-skinned Crosses rule over the white-skinned noughts and treat them like inferior beings. It shows how inequality and prejudice can force people into roles they do not want to be in and actions they don't want to take. This is a seriously thought provoking book and sometimes harsh as the two worlds of Sephy and Callum collide. It is at times heartbreaking, but even with all the sorrow the story is incredibly well paced and I was pulled along with each chapter.<br /><br />The content is brutal, but it has to be for the story to be authentic. It is also honest and doesn't hide from the fact that the consequences of racism and prejudice can create evil in the form of terrorism. A tale of race and equality, never patronising to it's target audience and giving us no answers to a world that's unforgiving and cruel. The ending is powerful, beautiful and devastating and I cried like a baby.<br /><br />Verdict:<br /><br />What can I say that I already haven't said. This is a remarkable novel; brilliantly written with complex characters, moving and thought provoking, full of pain, love and passion. I absolutely loved it and can't wait to read the rest in the series. I highly recommend this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17283885881851288669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer602908983" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17185484908738500168"><br/><br/><i>“Just remember, Callum when you’re floating up and up in your bubble, that bubbles have a habit of bursting. The higher you <b>climb</b>, the further you have to <b>fall</b>..."</i><br/><br/><br/>***2 stars*** This is my fourth time writing this review. Let's hope it gets done this time***<br/><br/><br/>It's time for...<br/><br/>*drumroll*<br/><br/> <i>Jenn's Pro/Con List!</i><br/><br/><br/> <b>
  <i>Pros:</i>
</b><br/><br/> 1. The dual POV. Sometimes when a character makes a stupid decision, you wonder "What the hell was he/she/it thinking?" Well, because this book was told from both Sephy and Callum's fir</span>
  <span id="freeText17185484908738500168" style="display:none"><br /><br /><i>“Just remember, Callum when you’re floating up and up in your bubble, that bubbles have a habit of bursting. The higher you <b>climb</b>, the further you have to <b>fall</b>..."</i><br /><br /><br />***2 stars*** This is my fourth time writing this review. Let's hope it gets done this time***<br /><br /><br />It's time for...<br /><br />*drumroll*<br /><br /> <i>Jenn's Pro/Con List!</i><br /><br /><br /> <b>
  <i>Pros:</i>
</b><br /><br /> 1. The dual POV. Sometimes when a character makes a stupid decision, you wonder "What the hell was he/she/it thinking?" Well, because this book was told from both Sephy and Callum's first-person point-of-view, you know exactly what they were thinking. It really does shed some light. You may not agree with what they did, but at least you know why they did it.<br /><br /> 2. The characters are realistic and complex. I especially liked Callum, because he was a realist, and smart, too. Sephy irritated me to no end because she was so naive. But then again, I'm pretty sure she was supposed to be that way. It would be weird if she were like Callum, because their circumstances are so different. <i>They</i> are so different.<br /><br />3. At least it was food for thought?<br /><br /> <b>
  <i>Cons:</i>
</b><br /><br /> 1. This was pretty much the story of the Civil Rights movement except racially reversed. I was hoping for something more imaginative. I already know about the <i>real</i> Civils Rights Movement, I don't need to read a re-hash ("re-hash" what a funny word) of it.<br /><br /> 2. Much of the plot was predictable. There were few, if any, surprises. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I predicted Lynette's suicide, Gabe joining the Liberation Militia, and Callum's dad's suicide quite easily. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /> 3. The cover of the book says "a thriller". Aren't thrillers supposed to be, you know, <i>thrilling</i>? I was very unthrilled, and maybe even a bit bored for the majority of this book. It was slow to progress.<br /><br /> 4. Damn that ending. <br /><br /><br />Final Comments:<br /> <br />I do not plan on continuing with this series. I'm just not engrossed enough. I was expecting something more original, or at least more exciting. So yeah, that pretty much sums it up. That's all I guess.<br /><br /> -JennTheAwesum</span>
  <a data-text-id="17185484908738500168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3829658678607148285" style="display:none">This is fiction for teenagers so it lacks real depth and could be at times described as a little contrived, but it's easy to read and provides an interesting insight into a world where race relations are the total reverse of the current reality. That said, I'm not sure what message this book was trying to convey, is the message that predjudice will always prevail, or that we should walk in our neighbours shoes before passing judgement. I hope it's the latter but I was left a little unclear, hopefully the remainder of the trilogy will reveal it for me.</span>

<div id="review_1609457405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609457405" />
    <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis"><img alt="Joey Woolfardis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490696206p2/4639825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1609457405?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joey Woolfardis" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis">Joey Woolfardis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552546324" href="/book/show/881512.Noughts_Crosses">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=ahreet">ahreet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=bairns">bairns</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=sterling">sterling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=bookshelf">bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=feminine">feminine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=ce21">ce21</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1609457405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2813930791906706606">Read as part of <a href='https://infiniteanddarling.co.uk/blogs/infinite-variety-books/the-infinite-variety-reading-challenge-part-one' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Infinite Variety Reading Challenge</a>, based on the BBC's Big Read Poll of 2003.<br/><br/>This is a very important book for what it is telling you and I think it's very important that the audience this book is written for are children and teenagers. Unfortunately, this means that I dislike it because of that, since there is no theme or amount of excellent writing that will make me enjoy a story that is narrated by annoying, self-centred "AH ME" teenagers.<br/><br/>The plot itself-the story arc that</span>
  <span id="freeText2813930791906706606" style="display:none">Read as part of <a href="https://infiniteanddarling.co.uk/blogs/infinite-variety-books/the-infinite-variety-reading-challenge-part-one" rel="nofollow noopener">The Infinite Variety Reading Challenge</a>, based on the BBC's Big Read Poll of 2003.<br /><br />This is a very important book for what it is telling you and I think it's very important that the audience this book is written for are children and teenagers. Unfortunately, this means that I dislike it because of that, since there is no theme or amount of excellent writing that will make me enjoy a story that is narrated by annoying, self-centred "AH ME" teenagers.<br /><br />The plot itself-the story arc that propels the book along-is pretty much a thin, Things That Happen, standard kind of plot that wasn't hugely appealing but kept the whole thing tied together quite nicely. There are a few surprises, but I'd wager they're nothing you can't find in half a dozen other novels that are of the dystopian nature.<br /><br />However, the themes of the book (racism and things relating to it) is exceptionally poignant and very important. It is at times obvious-which it needs to be-and sometimes blunt-which it needs to be-and often harsh-which it needs to be. I can't say I've read anything like this before but I couldn't help from feeling annoyed that it wasn't written with me in mind. I hated all the characters to the point that I really didn't care what happened to them, except as a whole society. I am definitely intrigued by this world and I think it's a very original unoriginal world and, despite the fact I am not the intended audience, it really did make me think.<br /><br />If you do enjoy Young Adult novels, or novels that have teenage protagonist who speak in the first person-either in diary form or not-then I strongly recommend this to you, I really do.<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.infiniteanddarling.co.uk/blogs/infinite-variety-books" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/infiniteANDdarling/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/infinitedarlin" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://uk.pinterest.com/infinitedarling/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> | <a href="https://www.infiniteanddarling.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Shop</a> | <a href="https://www.etsy.com/uk/shop/infiniteANDdarling" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2813930791906706606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650226401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4686936535148644491">Holy crap this was amazing! <br/><br/>I don't know how to categorise this book it's sort of a contemporary set in a world where history is alternate to our world's history but still pretty much the same. The only alternate aspect is that instead of light-skinned people always being in power and enslaving dark-skinned people, dark-skinned people (crosses) are in power and had in the past enslaved light-skinned people (noughts). <br/><br/>So this book is basically a mix of contemporary and dystopian and those are my </span>
  <span id="freeText4686936535148644491" style="display:none">Holy crap this was amazing! <br /><br />I don't know how to categorise this book it's sort of a contemporary set in a world where history is alternate to our world's history but still pretty much the same. The only alternate aspect is that instead of light-skinned people always being in power and enslaving dark-skinned people, dark-skinned people (crosses) are in power and had in the past enslaved light-skinned people (noughts). <br /><br />So this book is basically a mix of contemporary and dystopian and those are my two least favourite genres but I loved this book... just ponder that.<br /><br />This book was so good and touching and very thought provoking. The story in this first book had an entire arc and was wrapped up very well and enough so that this could be a stand alone. <br /><br />I loved this book 5/5 stars. I will re-read this in future.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=poc-narrator">poc-narrator</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755798195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13731952901486050005">3.5 stars.<br/><br/>So for the first hundred pages or so of this book, I was really frustrated by the lack of world building. Right up until the point where I was like "Oh shit, every damned book set in a world dominated by white people doesn't need world building to explain why white people are in charge of anything..." <br/><br/>Yeah. Check your privilege, white girl. <br/><br/>Anyway. There was eventually a small amount of world building, just enough to give a basic history of the planet. The world is great, the character</span>
  <span id="freeText13731952901486050005" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br />So for the first hundred pages or so of this book, I was really frustrated by the lack of world building. Right up until the point where I was like "Oh shit, every damned book set in a world dominated by white people doesn't need world building to explain why white people are in charge of anything..." <br /><br />Yeah. Check your privilege, white girl. <br /><br />Anyway. There was eventually a small amount of world building, just enough to give a basic history of the planet. The world is great, the characters are enjoyable, the writing was compelling. Really, my main gripe with this was that the chapters felt incredibly short most of the time, and it covers a LOT of time in one book. Like, when the book starts, Sephy is about to turn 14 and Callum is nearly 16. And at the end of the book, Sephy is...18?? Or nearly 18?? And Callum is 20. So that's a lot of time to cram into 480 pages. <br /><br />Anyway. The ending was a little abrupt, but I'm definitely interested to see how the series progresses from here, and the author's note about how the story was influenced by her reaction to the arrests of young black men definitely added another level to things. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13731952901486050005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3128875870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3128875870" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3128875870?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3128875870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7640092319072662682">I re-read this as it's this month's choice for my work book club and I have to admit I really enjoyed the re-read as it's been quite a long time since I read a contemporary, and a very long time since I picked this one up, even though it's one of my favourites. This story is gripping, emotional, shocking, sad, and tragic. There are many moments of happiness between Callum and Sephy, but there are also so many moments that their society makes them go through things that no child should have to fa</span>
  <span id="freeText7640092319072662682" style="display:none">I re-read this as it's this month's choice for my work book club and I have to admit I really enjoyed the re-read as it's been quite a long time since I read a contemporary, and a very long time since I picked this one up, even though it's one of my favourites. This story is gripping, emotional, shocking, sad, and tragic. There are many moments of happiness between Callum and Sephy, but there are also so many moments that their society makes them go through things that no child should have to face. <br /><br />If you haven't read it, you should :) Even if contemporary isn't usually your thing as it's a dystopian contemporary and I really love it 5*s.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3456362852" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3456362852" />
    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41243494-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605270057p2/41243494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3456362852?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/41243494-brittany">Brittany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780241324073" href="/book/show/37761152-noughts-crosses">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41243494-brittany?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41243494-brittany?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3456362852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14205248621950038953">“Why did I have to represent all noughts? Why couldn’t I just represent myself?”<br/><br/>I remember reading half of this book in school years ago and being obsessed with it, because of that I was worried as I’m a lot older now I wouldn’t actually enjoy it – but I should know better than to underestimate Malorie Blackman; she just smashes it every time with storylines.<br/><br/>The concept of this book is like a dystopian society where white people are the ones at the receiving end of systematic racism. It’s a dyst</span>
  <span id="freeText14205248621950038953" style="display:none">“Why did I have to represent all noughts? Why couldn’t I just represent myself?”<br /><br />I remember reading half of this book in school years ago and being obsessed with it, because of that I was worried as I’m a lot older now I wouldn’t actually enjoy it – but I should know better than to underestimate Malorie Blackman; she just smashes it every time with storylines.<br /><br />The concept of this book is like a dystopian society where white people are the ones at the receiving end of systematic racism. It’s a dystopian but also not – this book was so well executed and did an amazing job of exposing several truths about the society that we live in, the history, and the way racism still presents itself explicitly and implicitly. Honestly it is barely fiction – this stuff happened to Black people. If you’re outraged by the things that happen in this book, these are things that Black people had to live through not even that long ago. It’s horrifying. It is a hard to read book, it’s really uncomfortable, but it is full of so many eye opening and blatant truths that I think white readers especially need to hear. A really important series, especially for the YA genre and I will recommend this book happily in the future.<br /><br />It’s really fast paced which helped keep my attention, every chapter is full of mystery and intrigue I had so many questions I wanted answering so couldn’t put the book down. I will say though, for it’s pacing I do think it was perhaps a bit too fast, but then again there was clearly so much plot wise that needed to be included it kind of made sense. In my opinion, though, I would’ve preferred a slower moving plot with more suspense and build up. Alongside this, the ‘chapters’ didn’t really make sense at all and the constant shift in POV wasn’t really my cup of tea, I never felt overly connected to the characters because I didn’t get enough time with them.<br /><br />On this note, I really wished each character had more personality. I feel like the only thing I know about the two protagonists is that they are obsessed with each other; I know this is the focal point of the story, but they honestly have no other personality. I’m not sure whether this is intentional or an oversight, but it felt like such a shame to me. There were several points in this book intended to be shocking and really emotional but it didn’t have any impact on me at all because I don’t really love the characters. I just feel like I don’t know who any of them are which is a shame. <br /><br />A lot of dark subjects are broached in this book, and it does say it’s unsuitable for younger readers - I would definitely second that. I’d advise googling content warnings before delving into this series unknowingly because it is really dark. Some of it is done really well, some of it is a bit questionable and feels like it’s just thrown in for the drama. Like, there’s so much chaos in this book I don’t think a single character is happy or having an easy time of life it’s mad.<br /><br />All in all, I liked it and I like the storyline, I just think it’s a bit too full on and needed stripping back a bit. I would’ve also loved to connect more with the characters. Having said that, really intrigued to see where the series goes, and a perfect read for my Black History Month tbr!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14205248621950038953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('27RSGoplYSwCH7fyMULZ9auEJnHrgWLyj0NCp7jt7k7hkjvIMTuoRKU0A5PGt9MqfdvBuSUM7JXUPQQWda4c1A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fFKvp65ZiUWNjz4fI3+G5d3p85z24nDcfXwe30jIr/JGdMZ1FQdALSqkin7Uiow6C7YUVDhv/rsmAlhuhYtdaA==')})
  }
